Types of beauty; genetic you do not choose. Cosmetic which is how you modify your genetic appearance temporarily with outfits or makeup. Functional; exercise that makes you healthier and more able to do any desired paid or unpaid labors, a functional change to the body but will also almost always make you look healthier and make you look more capable. So the last is two desirable traits from exercise; health and capability of work...neither is beauty per se, but do make a person more desirable anyway. More esoteric beauty is the personality; it is wonderful to see someone almost give up...but they pause a moment and call on more reserves, and keep trying + succeed in something wonderful from that extra effort. So this is not beauty of a physical sort, but the sort of 'root for the person struggling, and be happy when they succeed' IE this really has nothing to do with species or genetics but more empathy and visceral happiness at others success. Is that too abstract for you to call beauty? Well for me it still applies. Similarly appreciating other personality traits that I personally like, makes an already cosmetically attractive person more likable and desirable. The opposite applies too; multiple people very attractive physically...I want nothing to do with because I dislike their personality. There are more examples; someone posing in stillness can be pretty from their deliberate pose even if they are so so in cosmetic appearance...IE it is the pose that is the pretty part not their body. Or an unattractive person, can be a beautiful person when dancing because how they dance is wonderful. Actions and choices thus increase or decrease overall attractiveness.

When I was a kid, until I was 10 years old, I thought I was the happiest kid on the planet.  I had friends, I got excellent grades, I had great relationships with teachers and with my family. But my school only went up to fourth grade and that was all over, the next year my class broke up and all my happiness and joy turned to ashes in my mouth. I discovered myself homosexual at the age of 11 and at that time it was still a huge taboo. I lost all my childhood friendships, my relatives started to demand traits of a heterosexual man showing interest in sports, which is something I don't like.  I suffered from loneliness as a homosexual from 11 to 18 years old. When I turned 18, I decided to explore the world and try to insert myself into the LGBTQIA+ community and I was only rejected and humiliated for being skinny and out of shape.  Since then, from the age of 18 to the age of 29, the problem in my life has been not being able to adapt to the fitness standard. I feel like my story is the story of the ugly duckling, with no happy ending. I think about suicide daily. This clip made me hopeful to see that subjects like fatphobia, skinnyphobia, aesthetic pressure can save lives and finally put an end to appearance prejudice.

I have heard of this song before but listening to this song today transformed my life.  My fiance opened this song for me because I have always struggled with body image due to the trauma experienced from my first boyfriend who used to tell me that "You are perfect - except just one thing. Too bad. You aren't beautiful." Don't ask me why I dated such a guy. Haven't we all been there? Falling in love with someone who didn't deserve you but still managed to be fooled by the blindness of that love...  It has been 9 years since I first heard those toxic words. Yet, I still repeat it to myself and act as though I could never be beautiful. I even doubt other people when they call me beautiful. Are they just providing lip service? Are they saying it just because they are nice? I know it is ridiculous to give so much credibility to such negativity. But sometimes... the mind moves on it own and takes us away from where we deserve to be.  Recently, I have been extremely insecure in the process of choosing wedding dresses. I cried many times fearing that my "non-standard" body wouldn't be able to fit into all these beautiful dresses.   My fiance has been very patient, caring,  and loving throughout all these. He ensures me that I am beautiful as I am. I am beautiful - whether in a wedding dress, casual dress, professional dress, pajamas, or without any clothes. More importantly, I am beautiful as his lover, as my parents' daughter, as my brother's sister, as my close friends' friend... I am beautiful not just because of how I look with certain clothes or without any clothes, but because of who I am in the inside. He opened this song for me, looked into my tear-filled eyes, held me tight as I trembled, and held my hands as I felt weak and insecure.   At that moment, I remember a conversation with my host mother. I once asked her, "How did you come to believe in God?" She said that she read the Bible in college and thought that "Wouldn't it be nice if I can believe in all these?" And just like that - she believed and she continued to believe until today. And that belief has guided her for the better.  Wouldn't it be nice if I can believe in my fiance's sincere gaze, strong embrace, and loving words? Wouldn't it be nice if I can let myself free of the haunting evil spirit telling myself I am not beautiful? Wouldn't it be nice if I can believe in my worth and start telling myself that I am beautiful as I am today?  I want to believe.   And I shall believe.

My stance on the whole trans thing: these children today are lacking healthy social circles to feel accepted in, good role models, and people close to them that are trusting so that they can talk out their struggles. Adolescence is a tough time for everyone, developing body changes are scary. When parents are not there to be real with their children about the reality of these changes, it can make for a much tougher time on their kids.   The way someone acts, or the clothes they wear, their hairstyle or their hobbies, or any other personality traits, does not correlate with their sex. Sex and gender identity are mutually exclusive.  Youth today should understand that the key to freedom of identity expression is to challenge old societal stereotypes/definitions of what a girl or boy ought to look and act like. Girls ought to be free to be tomboys, while it having nothing to do with being any less of a girl; and vice versa for boys. They can FEEL and ACT and LOOK any way they so choose, without it correlating to a problem with their natural body. Liking things that society labels as traditionally "for men" should never mean that there is something wrong with a woman. How you feel, or your mental state, have nothing to do with your physical body.  Stemming from that, if you have a mental issue, messing with your physical body or taking health destroying hormones to try and change it, will never help with the mental issues you've been having. If anything, going through body augmentation will leave most youth frustrated because it wasn't the solution to their problems. The solution is to speak to genuinely understanding people or a therapist, work through your demons, and tell off society's stupid stereotypes about gender identity.

Wow. I was uhh... Expecting something better? And looking at the comments, I guess I was the only one. The song still slaps, but this video is very ... well. Not good?  One, it seems to be aiming its message almost exclusively at the Daniel Tiger audience? The original spoke more to teenagers and young adults, which made sense as one's concern with their body tends to skyrocket at the age one actually is developing their body, while I don't recall that being as much of a concern for 9-year-olds. Like, this video literally has tiny children getting prepped for facial reconstruction surgery, as if there is some epidemic of elementary grade kids demanding to have face lifts and eye-tucks. Who the fuck is this for?  Secondly, it seems kind of weird that the 2002 version of the video had heavy LGBTQ representation while the 2022 version dismisses their existence? That seems kind of backwards. Given how the original was among the only positive trans representation on television at the time, it seems like at a time when that community is finally being given attention, one would double down on that representation?  Third, the way these tiny children are being directed to hold their phones, makes it appear as if they were instructed by a person who has never held a cellphone before. No one holds a phone that far away from their face for that long. Their arm would get tired. Especially if they have these little string-bean tiny children arms. Also â€” the bleeding phone at the end? The heavy handed attempts to paint cell phones as this evil little box both makes Christina give off boomer vibes at 41, but also ignores the fact that body dysmorphia and eating disorders have existed long before cell phones (hence the existence of her original video). Everything about this video seems to be from the perspective of someone so old that they can't tell the difference between teenagers and 10-year-olds, that they are incapable of relating to their intended audience and that they have decided that this song is no longer about encouraging those who feel inadequate to love themselves, but rather condemning the existence of technology.  But again. Clearly mine is a lone voice in a sea of praise, so I could be entirely wrong.

A year after this was originally released, I was sectioned for four months with anorexia. I remember another, much sicker, girl in the hospital would literally play this on repeat and I would hear it echoing into my room. I would hardly speak to the other girl, as we both hardly spoke to anyone but the hearing song made me feel slightly connected to her and her pain, I wanted her to get better and stop feeling what I was feeling. When the song played, my overwhelming loneliness soften just a little, as I briefly understood it wasnâ€™t just me struggling with my emotions and intense dislike for myself.  I feel like songs like this often help us give a voice for our experiences whilst we canâ€™t talk. The artist lends us theirs until we find our own, until we find our words. Itâ€™s one of the ways we can put some of the puzzle pieces together. I see music is a vessel for that, and therefore holds us in our most lonely hours, numbing the pain briefly, helping us through the night. By morning, we may have a little better understanding of our experiences or maybe we just had a brief painkiller.  But the connection to another, knowing somewhere out there, is trying to work out the same vortex of emotions inside, is one of the most important things music can give us.  It breaks my heart that kids are going through the same cycle as I did, and that the world is encouraging it much more with social media, rather than finding a way to reduce the harm itâ€™s causing. We may heal but there is damage that will always remain from it.
